Section 1:
Introduced Version
_____
DIGEST OF INTRODUCED BILL
Citations Affected: IC 4-3-23; IC 4-22-2-28.1; IC 4-23-5.5;
IC 5-28-17-6; IC 13-11-2; IC 13-12; IC 13-13; IC 13-14; IC 13-15;
IC 13-16; IC 13-17; IC 13-18; IC 13-19; IC 13-20; IC 13-20.5;
IC 13-21; IC 13-22; IC 13-23; IC 13-24-1; IC 13-25-5; IC 13-26;
IC 13-27; IC 13-28; IC 13-29-1-13; IC 13-30.
Synopsis: Indiana department of environmental management.
Amends, repeals, or adds certain terms. Makes certain changes
concerning the purpose, structure, and powers of the department of
environmental management or the environmental rules board. Makes
certain changes to various boards or funds. Eliminates or amends
rulemaking provisions. Makes certain changes to hearing and
permitting processes. Changes or eliminates certain reporting
requirements. Makes various changes to the water pollution statutes.
Makes various changes to the solid waste and hazardous waste
management statutes. Moves the Indiana recycling market development
board to Title 13. Repeals or amends various sections regarding: (1)
hazardous substances; (2) the voluntary remediation programs; (3)
regional water districts; and (4) citizen lawsuits. Makes conforming
and technical changes.
Effective: July 1, 2026.
Niemeyer
January 8, 2026, read first time and referred to Committee on Environmental Affairs.
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150
Introduced
Second Regular Session of the 124th General Assembly (2026)
PRINTING CODE. Amendments: Whenever an existing statute (or a section of the Indiana
Constitution) is being amended, the text of the existing provision will appear in this style type,
additions will appear in this style type, and deletions will appear in this style type.
Additions: Whenever a new statutory provision is being enacted (or a new constitutional
provision adopted), the text of the new provision will appear in this style type. Also, the
word NEW will appear in that style type in the introductory clause of each SECTION that adds
a new provision to the Indiana Code or the Indiana Constitution.
Conflict reconciliation: Text in a statute in this style type or this style type reconciles conflicts
between statutes enacted by the 2025 Regular Session of the General Assembly.
SENATE BILL No. 277
A BILL FOR AN ACT to amend the Indiana Code concerning
environmental law and to make an appropriation.
Be it enacted by the General Assembly of the State of Indiana:

7 AS A NEW SECTION TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE JULY
8 1, 2026]: Sec. 11. (a) The Indiana energy efficiency loan fund is
9 established for the purpose of assisting Indiana industries and
10 governing bodies (as defined in IC 36-1-12.5-1.5) in undertaking

12 board.
13 (b) Sources of money for the fund consist of the following:
14 (1) Appropriations from the general assembly.
15 (2) Repayment proceeds, including interest, of loans made
16 from the fund.
17 (3) Donations, gifts, and money received from any other
18 source, including transfers from other funds or accounts.
19 (c) Money remaining in the fund at the end of a state fiscal year
20 does not revert to the state general fund.
21 (d) The treasurer of state shall invest the money in the fund not
22 currently needed to meet the obligations of the fund in the same
23 manner as other public funds may be invested. Interest that
24 accrues from these investments shall be deposited in the fund.
25 (e) The board shall establish:
26 (1) amounts, terms, and interest rates for loans under this
27 section; and
28 (2) criteria for awarding loans under this section.
29 (f) A person, business, governing body, or manufacturer that
30 wants a loan from the fund must file an application in the manner
31 prescribed by the board.

6 rule identifies an element of the proposed rule that imposes a restriction

8 requirement imposed under federal law, the proposed rule shall not
9 become effective under this chapter until the adjournment sine die of
10 the regular session of the general assembly that begins after the
11 department provides the notice.
12 (c) Subsection (b) does not prohibit or restrict the commissioner, the

36 (A) The application of lime to break down PCB.
37 (B) The low temperature thermal disorption process.
38 (C) Disorption and vaporization extraction.
39 (D) Plasma torch technology.
40 (E) Bacterial remediation.
41 (2) Other technologies identified by the commissioner as having
42 possible value in the treatment or disposal of PCB in Indiana.

32 diversion of valuable raw materials for procurement to identified
33 Indiana based end markets as a commodity.

37 (2) award of funds necessary to implement the project.
38 The duration of the project may not exceed four (4) years after the date

40 (e) The project established under this section shall commence a
41 second round of grants within one (1) year after the first round of
42 grants are awarded to the selected projects. Applicants selected for a
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150

1 grant during the first round of grants may apply for a grant during the

13 SECTION 245. IC 13-20-27 IS ADDED TO THE INDIANA CODE
14 AS A NEW CHAPTER TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE
15 JULY 1, 2026]:
16 Chapter 27. Indiana Recycling Market Development Board
17 Sec. 1. (a) The Indiana recycling market development board is
18 created and constitutes a public instrumentality of the state.
19 (b) The board consists of eight (8) members, who shall be
20 appointed by the governor for four (4) year terms. The governor's
21 appointees shall be chosen from among representatives of:
22 (1) the waste management industry;
23 (2) the recycling industry;
24 (3) Indiana universities and colleges with expertise in
25 recycling research and development;
26 (4) industrial and commercial consumers of recycled
27 feedstock;
28 (5) environmental groups; and
29 (6) private citizens with a special interest in recycling.
30 In appointing individuals under this subsection, the governor may
31 consider geographic location, political affiliation, and other factors
32 to ensure viewpoints are fairly balanced in terms of points of view
33 represented on the board.
34 (c) A member may not serve more than two (2) consecutive four
35 (4) year terms. The term of each member of the board continues
36 until a successor is appointed.
37 (d) A vacancy in the office of an appointed member, other than
38 by expiration, shall be filled in like manner as the original
39 appointment for the remainder of the term of that retiring
40 member. Appointed members may be removed by the governor at
41 any time with or without cause.
42 (e) The board shall have seven (7) ex officio advisory members
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150
125
1 as follows:
2 (1) The governor.
3 (2) The director of the department of natural resources.
4 (3) The commissioner.
5 (4) Two (2) members from the house of representatives of
6 opposite political parties appointed by the speaker of the
7 house of representatives for two (2) year terms that expire
8 June 30 of each odd-numbered year.
9 (5) Two (2) members from the senate of opposite political
10 parties appointed by the president pro tempore of the senate
11 for two (2) year terms that expire June 30 of each
12 odd-numbered year.
13 (f) The department shall serve as the staff of the board.
14 (g) An ex officio advisory member identified in subsection (e)
15 may, in writing, designate a representative to serve in an advisory
16 capacity when the ex officio member is unable to attend a board
17 meeting.
18 (h) The terms of the members of the board appointed by the
19 governor under subsection (b) expire as follows:
20 (1) For four (4) of the members, as determined by the
21 governor, December 31, 2025, and every fourth year
22 thereafter.
23 (2) For four (4) of the members, as determined by the
24 governor, December 31, 2027, and every fourth year
25 thereafter.
26 Sec. 2. (a) Each member of the board who is not a state
27 employee is entitled to the minimum salary per diem provided by
28 IC 4-10-11-2.1(b). The member is also entitled to reimbursement
29 for mileage, traveling expenses as provided under IC 4-13-1-4, and
30 other expenses actually incurred in connection with the member's
31 duties as provided in the state policies and procedures established
32 by the Indiana department of administration and approved by the
33 budget agency.
34 (b) Each member of the board who is a state employee is entitled
35 to reimbursement for traveling expenses as provided under
36 IC 4-13-1-4 and other expenses actually incurred in connection
37 with the member's duties as provided in the state policies and
38 procedures established by the Indiana department of
39 administration and approved by the budget agency.
40 (c) Each member of the board who is a member of the general
41 assembly is entitled to receive the same per diem, mileage, and
42 travel allowances paid to members of the general assembly serving
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150
126
1 on interim study committees established by the legislative council.
2 Per diem, mileage, and travel allowances paid under this
3 subsection shall be paid from appropriations made to the
4 legislative council or the legislative services agency.
5 (d) Expenses paid under subsections (a) and (b) shall be paid
6 from appropriations made to the department.
7 Sec. 3. The governor shall appoint one (1) of the appointed
8 members as chairperson. Four (4) members of the board shall
9 constitute a quorum and the affirmative vote of a majority of the
10 membership shall be necessary for any action taken by the board.
11 A vacancy in the membership of the board does not impair the
12 right of the quorum to act.
13 Sec. 4. A member of the board must disclose to the board and
14 the department any interest in a project the board may be
15 considering for action. The board shall determine whether that
16 member shall be allowed to participate in activities related to that
17 project.
18 Sec. 5. (a) The board may do any of the following:
19 (1) Adopt procedures for the conduct of its business.
20 (2) Meet at least twice per year. The meetings shall be open to
21 the public, conducted in accordance with IC 5-14-1.5, and
22 have official minutes recorded for public scrutiny.
23 (3) Report annually in an electronic format under IC 5-14-6
24 to the legislative council concerning:
25 (A) the projects in which it has participated and is
26 currently participating with a complete list of expenditures
27 for those projects; and
28 (B) the information obtained through the recycling activity
29 reports submitted to the commissioner under IC 13-20-25
30 concerning the calendar year most recently ended.
31 (4) Annually prepare an administrative budget for review by
32 the budget agency and the budget committee.
33 (5) Keep proper records of accounts and make an annual
34 report of its condition to the state board of accounts.
35 (6) Receive petitions and make determinations under
36 IC 13-20.5-2-2.
37 (b) The board shall consider projects involving the creation of
38 the following:
39 (1) Markets for products made from recycled materials.
40 (2) New products made from recycled materials.
41 (c) The board may promote, fund, and encourage programs
42 facilitating the development and implementation of waste
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150
127
1 reduction, reuse, and recycling in Indiana.
2 Sec. 6. The board, upon approval by the governor and the
3 budget agency, may make the following expenditures:
4 (1) Matching grants to federal, state, and local governmental
5 agencies for research and development of:
6 (A) recycling projects; and
7 (B) recycling market development projects;
8 in Indiana.
9 (2) Matching grants to individuals, corporations, limited

14 individuals and organizations specified in subdivision (1) or
15 (2).
16 (4) Contractual services for recycling and recycling market
17 research and development programs.
18 (5) Other projects and expenses consistent with this chapter.
19 Sec. 7. The board does not have the authority to exercise the
20 power of eminent domain.
21 Sec. 8. The board may:
22 (1) on behalf of the state, receive and accept grants, gifts, and
23 contributions from public agencies, including the federal

26 corporation, for the purpose of researching and developing

33 (3) accept applications from private and public sources for

35 (4) provide funding for studies, research projects, and other

39 (5) deposit funds not currently needed to meet the obligations

42 (6) participate in or sponsor programs, conferences, or
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150
128
1 seminars aimed at assisting the state in promoting recycling
2 market development.
3 Sec. 9. (a) The Indiana recycling promotion and assistance fund
4 is established. The purpose of the fund is to promote and assist
5 recycling throughout Indiana by focusing economic development
6 efforts on businesses and projects involving recycling. The fund
7 shall be administered by the board.
8 (b) Sources of money for the fund consist of the following:
9 (1) Appropriations from the general assembly.
10 (2) Repayment proceeds of loans made from the fund.
11 (3) Gifts and donations.
12 (4) Money from the solid waste management fund.
13 (c) Money remaining in the fund at the end of a state fiscal year
14 does not revert to the state general fund.
15 (d) The board may use money in the fund to make loans to
16 assist:
17 (1) persons in establishing new recycling businesses;
18 (2) in the expansion of existing recycling businesses; and
19 (3) manufacturers in retrofitting equipment necessary to
20 reuse or recycle secondary materials.
21 (e) The board shall establish loan:
22 (1) amounts;
23 (2) terms; and
24 (3) interest rates.
25 (f) The board may use money in the fund to make grants for
26 research and development projects involving recycling. The board
27 shall establish amounts for grants.
28 (g) A person, business, or manufacturer that wants a grant or
29 loan from the fund must file an application with the board.
30 (h) The board shall establish criteria for awarding grants and
31 loans under this section.
32 (i) To implement the central Indiana waste diversion project as
33 described in IC 13-20-26, the board shall award not more than four
34 million dollars ($4,000,000) in total to applicants chosen to
35 participate in the project based on:
36 (1) the recommendations of the department after conducting
37 an evaluation of the proposals submitted under IC 13-20-26-2;
38 and
39 (2) the requirements set forth in subsection (j).
40 (j) In awarding the funds described in subsection (i), the board
41 shall:
42 (1) consult with the department when reviewing the proposals
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150
129
1 under IC 13-20-26-2;
2 (2) consider the:
3 (A) type; and
4 (B) amount;
5 of waste that is proposed to be diverted during the project
6 under IC 13-20-26;
7 (3) consider the potential for productive reuse of the waste

16 program year thereafter, the registration fee is equal to two thousand
17 five hundred dollars ($2,500).
18 (c) In addition to the registration fee under subsection (a), a
19 manufacturer that registers under IC 13-20.5-1 and fails to meet the
20 recycling goal under IC 13-20.5-4-1 is subject to a variable recycling
21 fee for each program year that ends on March 31 of 2013 or December
22 31 of a later year. Not later than September 1, the department shall
23 provide a statement to each manufacturer liable for the variable
24 recycling fee that states at least the following:
25 (1) The amount of the fee determined under subsection (d).
26 (2) The method of calculation of the fee.
27 (3) The due date of the fee.
28 (4) The opportunity to petition under section 2 of this chapter.
29 The department shall deposit the fee in the Indiana recycling promotion
30 and assistance fund established by IC 4-23-5.5-14. IC 13-20-27-9.
31 (d) The amount of the variable recycling fee, if applicable, is the
32 amount determined in STEP FOUR of the following formula:
33 STEP ONE: Multiply the number of pounds of the manufacturer's
34 video display devices sold to households during the immediately
35 preceding program year, as reported in the manufacturer's
36 registration for the program year under IC 13-20.5-1-1(c)(4), by
37 the proportion of sales of video display devices required to be
38 recycled under IC 13-20.5-4-1.
39 STEP TWO: Subject to subsection (e), add the number of pounds
40 of covered electronic devices recycled by the manufacturer from
41 covered entities during the immediately preceding program year,
42 as reported to the department under IC 13-20.5-3-1(a), to the
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150
131
1 number of recycling credits the manufacturer elects to use to
2 calculate the variable recycling fee, as reported to the department
3 under IC 13-20.5-3-1(b)(2).
4 STEP THREE: Subtract the number of pounds determined in
5 STEP TWO from the number of pounds determined in STEP
6 ONE.
7 STEP FOUR: Multiply the greater of zero (0) or the number of
8 pounds determined in STEP THREE by the per pound cost of
9 recycling established as follows:
10 (A) Forty cents ($0.40) per pound for manufacturers that
11 recycle less than fifty percent (50%) of the number of pounds
12 determined in STEP ONE.
13 (B) Thirty cents ($0.30) per pound for manufacturers that
14 recycle at least fifty percent (50%) but less than ninety percent
15 (90%) of the number of pounds determined in STEP ONE.
16 (C) Twenty cents ($0.20) per pound for manufacturers that
17 recycle at least ninety percent (90%) of the number of pounds
18 determined in STEP ONE.
19 (e) The following apply to the number of pounds of covered
20 electronic devices recycled by the manufacturer from covered entities
21 during the immediately preceding program year for purposes of
22 subsection (d), STEP TWO:
23 (1) Except as provided in subdivision (3), the number is
24 multiplied by one and one-tenth (1.1) to the extent that the
25 covered electronic devices were recycled in Indiana.
26 (2) Except as provided in subdivision (3), the number is
27 multiplied by one and five-tenths (1.5) to the extent that the
28 covered electronic devices were recycled from covered entities
29 not located in a metropolitan statistical area, as defined by the
30 federal Office of Management and Budget.
31 (3) The number is multiplied by one and six-tenths (1.6) to the
32 extent that the covered electronic devices were:
33 (A) recycled from covered entities not located in a
34 metropolitan statistical area, as defined by the federal Office
35 of Management and Budget; and
36 (B) recycled in Indiana.
37 (f) A manufacturer may retain recycling credits to be added, in
38 whole or in part, to the actual number of pounds of covered electronic
39 devices recycled by the manufacturer from covered entities during the
40 immediately preceding program year, as reported to the department
41 under IC 13-20.5-3-1(a), during any of the three (3) immediately
42 succeeding program years. A manufacturer may sell all or any part of
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150
132
1 its recycling credits to another manufacturer, at a price negotiated by
2 the parties, and the other manufacturer may use the credits in the same
3 manner.
4 (g) A manufacturer may not be charged a registration fee or a
5 variable recycling fee for any year in which the combined number of
6 video display devices produced by the manufacturer for sale to
7 households is less than one hundred (100).

20 (f) Notwithstanding the maximum fine provisions of IC 35-50-3-2,
21 criminal fines for a person convicted of an offense described in
22 subsection (e) shall be assessable in a maximum amount of not less
23 than ten thousand dollars ($10,000) per day per violation.
24 (g) A person who willfully or recklessly violates any applicable
25 standards or limitations of IC 13-18-8 commits a Class B misdemeanor.
26 (h) A person who willfully or recklessly violates any applicable
27 standards or limitations of IC 13-18-9, IC 13-18-10, or IC 13-18-10.5
28 commits a Class C misdemeanor.
29 (i) A person who:
30 (1) knowingly commits any act described in subsection (a), (c), or
31 (e); and
32 (2) knows that commission of the act places another person in
33 imminent danger of death or serious bodily injury;
34 commits a Level 4 felony. However, the offense is a Level 3 felony if
35 it results in serious bodily injury to any person, and a Level 2 felony if
36 it results in the death of any person.
37 (j) It shall be a defense to an offense described in subsection (i) that
38 the person charged:
39 (1) did not know; or
40 (2) could not reasonably have been expected to know;
41 that the violation would place another person in imminent danger or
42 threat of serious bodily injury. For the purposes of subsection (i), a
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150
175
1 person is responsible only for the person's own actual awareness or
2 actual belief, and knowledge by another person may not be attributed
3 to the person.
4 (k) The penalties under this section apply regardless of whether a
5 person uses electronic submissions or paper documents to accomplish
6 the actions described in this section.

Raw Text:
Introduced Version
SENATE BILL No. 277
_____
DIGEST OF INTRODUCED BILL
Citations Affected: IC 4-3-23; IC 4-22-2-28.1; IC 4-23-5.5;
IC 5-28-17-6; IC 13-11-2; IC 13-12; IC 13-13; IC 13-14; IC 13-15;
IC 13-16; IC 13-17; IC 13-18; IC 13-19; IC 13-20; IC 13-20.5;
IC 13-21; IC 13-22; IC 13-23; IC 13-24-1; IC 13-25-5; IC 13-26;
IC 13-27; IC 13-28; IC 13-29-1-13; IC 13-30.
Synopsis: Indiana department of environmental management.
Amends, repeals, or adds certain terms. Makes certain changes
concerning the purpose, structure, and powers of the department of
environmental management or the environmental rules board. Makes
certain changes to various boards or funds. Eliminates or amends
rulemaking provisions. Makes certain changes to hearing and
permitting processes. Changes or eliminates certain reporting
requirements. Makes various changes to the water pollution statutes.
Makes various changes to the solid waste and hazardous waste
management statutes. Moves the Indiana recycling market development
board to Title 13. Repeals or amends various sections regarding: (1)
hazardous substances; (2) the voluntary remediation programs; (3)
regional water districts; and (4) citizen lawsuits. Makes conforming
and technical changes.
Effective: July 1, 2026.
Niemeyer
January 8, 2026, read first time and referred to Committee on Environmental Affairs.
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150

Introduced
Second Regular Session of the 124th General Assembly (2026)
PRINTING CODE. Amendments: Whenever an existing statute (or a section of the Indiana
Constitution) is being amended, the text of the existing provision will appear in this style type,
additions will appear in this style type, and deletions will appear in this style type.
Additions: Whenever a new statutory provision is being enacted (or a new constitutional
provision adopted), the text of the new provision will appear in this style type. Also, the
word NEW will appear in that style type in the introductory clause of each SECTION that adds
a new provision to the Indiana Code or the Indiana Constitution.
Conflict reconciliation: Text in a statute in this style type or this style type reconciles conflicts
between statutes enacted by the 2025 Regular Session of the General Assembly.

24 (2) Assure for all citizens of Indiana safe, healthful, productive,

27 without degradation, risk to health or safety, or other undesirable
28 and unintended consequences.

30 our national heritage and maintain, wherever possible, an
31 environment that supports diversity and variety of individual
32 choice.

34 will permit Maintain high standards of living and a wise sharing
35 of life's amenities.
36 (6) Enhance the quality of renewable resources and approach the
37 maximum attainable recycling of depletable resources.
38 SECTION 50. IC 13-12-4-5, AS AMENDED BY P.L.133-2012,
39 SECTION 71, IS AMENDED TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE
40 JULY 1, 2026]: Sec. 5. To the fullest extent possible:
41 (1) the policies, rules, and statutes of the state shall be interpreted
42 and administered in accordance with the policies set forth in this
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150

21
1 chapter; and
2 (2) all state agencies shall do the following:
3 (A) Use a systematic, interdisciplinary approach that will
4 ensure the integrated use of the natural and social sciences and
5 the environmental design arts in planning and decision making
6 that may have an impact on the environment.
7 (B) Identify and develop methods and procedures that will
8 ensure that unquantified environmental amenities and values
9 may be given appropriate consideration in decision making
10 along with economic and technical considerations.
11 (C) Include in every recommendation or report on proposals
12 for legislation and other major state actions significantly
13 affecting the quality of the human environment a detailed
14 statement by the responsible official on the following:
15 (i) The environmental impact of the proposed action.
16 (ii) Any adverse environmental effects that cannot be
17 avoided should the proposal be implemented.
18 (iii) Alternatives to the proposed action.
19 (iv) The relationship between local short term uses of the
20 environment and the maintenance and enhancement of long
21 term productivity.
22 (v) Any irreversible and irretrievable commitments of
23 resources that would be involved if the proposed action
24 should be implemented.
25 Before making a detailed statement, the responsible state
26 official shall consult with and obtain the comments of each
27 state agency that has jurisdiction by law or special expertise
28 with respect to any environmental impact involved. Copies of
29 the statement and the comments and views of the appropriate
30 federal, state, and local agencies that are authorized to develop
31 and enforce environmental standards shall be made available
32 to the governor and to the public and must accompany the
33 proposal through the agency review processes. The board shall
34 by rule define the actions that constitute a major state action
35 significantly affecting the quality of the human environment.
36 (D) Study, develop, and describe appropriate alternatives to
37 recommend courses of action in any proposal that involves
38 unresolved conflicts concerning alternative uses of available
39 resources.
40 (E) Recognize the long range character of environmental
41 problems and, where consistent with the policy of the state,
42 lend appropriate support to initiatives, resolutions, and
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150

22
1 programs designed to maximize state cooperation in
2 anticipating and preventing a decline in the quality of the
3 environment.
4 (F) Make available to counties, municipalities, institutions,
5 and individuals advice and information useful in restoring,
6 maintaining, and enhancing the quality of the environment.
7 (G) Initiate and use ecological information in the planning and
8 development of resource oriented projects.

33 approaches to environmental protection:
34 (1) clean manufacturing; or

36 SECTION 55. IC 13-12-5-2 IS REPEALED [EFFECTIVE JULY 1,
37 2026]. Sec. 2. Clean manufacturing consists of economically feasible
38 practices that reduce, avoid, or eliminate the unnecessary use of
39 harmful industrial materials and the generation of industrial wastes,
40 pollutants, emissions, and discharges at the point of production. Clean
41 manufacturing practices are limited to the following:
42 (1) Product reformulation.
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150

23
1 (2) Input substitution.
2 (3) Equipment redesign.
3 (4) Improved operations and procedures.
4 SECTION 56. IC 13-12-5-3 IS REPEALED [EFFECTIVE JULY 1,
5 2026]. Sec. 3. Waste management or pollution control consists of
6 environmental protection practices employed after industrial wastes,
7 pollutants, discharges, and emissions have been generated. Waste
8 management or pollution control practices include the following:
9 (1) Waste storage and waste transportation.
10 (2) Waste treatment, including the following:
11 (A) Detoxification.
12 (B) Incineration.
13 (C) Biological treatment.
14 (3) Land disposal of wastes.
15 (4) Recycling.
16 (5) Burning waste as fuels.
17 (6) Dispersal of waste into air or water.
18 (7) Dewatering of waste.

42 (B) Persons that are located in Indiana but are not recyclers,

1 including persons who may employ the recyclable material as

13 SECTION 245. IC 13-20-27 IS ADDED TO THE INDIANA CODE
14 AS A NEW CHAPTER TO READ AS FOLLOWS [EFFECTIVE
15 JULY 1, 2026]:
16 Chapter 27. Indiana Recycling Market Development Board
17 Sec. 1. (a) The Indiana recycling market development board is
18 created and constitutes a public instrumentality of the state.
19 (b) The board consists of eight (8) members, who shall be
20 appointed by the governor for four (4) year terms. The governor's
21 appointees shall be chosen from among representatives of:
22 (1) the waste management industry;
23 (2) the recycling industry;
24 (3) Indiana universities and colleges with expertise in
25 recycling research and development;
26 (4) industrial and commercial consumers of recycled
27 feedstock;
28 (5) environmental groups; and
29 (6) private citizens with a special interest in recycling.
30 In appointing individuals under this subsection, the governor may
31 consider geographic location, political affiliation, and other factors
32 to ensure viewpoints are fairly balanced in terms of points of view
33 represented on the board.
34 (c) A member may not serve more than two (2) consecutive four
35 (4) year terms. The term of each member of the board continues
36 until a successor is appointed.
37 (d) A vacancy in the office of an appointed member, other than
38 by expiration, shall be filled in like manner as the original
39 appointment for the remainder of the term of that retiring
40 member. Appointed members may be removed by the governor at
41 any time with or without cause.
42 (e) The board shall have seven (7) ex officio advisory members
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150

125
1 as follows:
2 (1) The governor.
3 (2) The director of the department of natural resources.
4 (3) The commissioner.
5 (4) Two (2) members from the house of representatives of
6 opposite political parties appointed by the speaker of the
7 house of representatives for two (2) year terms that expire
8 June 30 of each odd-numbered year.
9 (5) Two (2) members from the senate of opposite political
10 parties appointed by the president pro tempore of the senate
11 for two (2) year terms that expire June 30 of each
12 odd-numbered year.
13 (f) The department shall serve as the staff of the board.
14 (g) An ex officio advisory member identified in subsection (e)
15 may, in writing, designate a representative to serve in an advisory
16 capacity when the ex officio member is unable to attend a board
17 meeting.
18 (h) The terms of the members of the board appointed by the
19 governor under subsection (b) expire as follows:
20 (1) For four (4) of the members, as determined by the
21 governor, December 31, 2025, and every fourth year
22 thereafter.
23 (2) For four (4) of the members, as determined by the
24 governor, December 31, 2027, and every fourth year
25 thereafter.
26 Sec. 2. (a) Each member of the board who is not a state
27 employee is entitled to the minimum salary per diem provided by
28 IC 4-10-11-2.1(b). The member is also entitled to reimbursement
29 for mileage, traveling expenses as provided under IC 4-13-1-4, and
30 other expenses actually incurred in connection with the member's
31 duties as provided in the state policies and procedures established
32 by the Indiana department of administration and approved by the
33 budget agency.
34 (b) Each member of the board who is a state employee is entitled
35 to reimbursement for traveling expenses as provided under
36 IC 4-13-1-4 and other expenses actually incurred in connection
37 with the member's duties as provided in the state policies and
38 procedures established by the Indiana department of
39 administration and approved by the budget agency.
40 (c) Each member of the board who is a member of the general
41 assembly is entitled to receive the same per diem, mileage, and
42 travel allowances paid to members of the general assembly serving
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150

126
1 on interim study committees established by the legislative council.
2 Per diem, mileage, and travel allowances paid under this
3 subsection shall be paid from appropriations made to the
4 legislative council or the legislative services agency.
5 (d) Expenses paid under subsections (a) and (b) shall be paid
6 from appropriations made to the department.
7 Sec. 3. The governor shall appoint one (1) of the appointed
8 members as chairperson. Four (4) members of the board shall
9 constitute a quorum and the affirmative vote of a majority of the
10 membership shall be necessary for any action taken by the board.
11 A vacancy in the membership of the board does not impair the
12 right of the quorum to act.
13 Sec. 4. A member of the board must disclose to the board and
14 the department any interest in a project the board may be
15 considering for action. The board shall determine whether that
16 member shall be allowed to participate in activities related to that
17 project.
18 Sec. 5. (a) The board may do any of the following:
19 (1) Adopt procedures for the conduct of its business.
20 (2) Meet at least twice per year. The meetings shall be open to

22 have official minutes recorded for public scrutiny.

33 (5) Keep proper records of accounts and make an annual
34 report of its condition to the state board of accounts.
35 (6) Receive petitions and make determinations under
36 IC 13-20.5-2-2.
37 (b) The board shall consider projects involving the creation of
38 the following:
39 (1) Markets for products made from recycled materials.
40 (2) New products made from recycled materials.
41 (c) The board may promote, fund, and encourage programs
42 facilitating the development and implementation of waste
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150

1 reduction, reuse, and recycling in Indiana.

2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150

3 Sec. 9. (a) The Indiana recycling promotion and assistance fund
4 is established. The purpose of the fund is to promote and assist
5 recycling throughout Indiana by focusing economic development
6 efforts on businesses and projects involving recycling. The fund
7 shall be administered by the board.
8 (b) Sources of money for the fund consist of the following:
9 (1) Appropriations from the general assembly.

16 assist:

22 (1) amounts;
23 (2) terms; and
24 (3) interest rates.

26 research and development projects involving recycling. The board
27 shall establish amounts for grants.

29 loan from the fund must file an application with the board.
30 (h) The board shall establish criteria for awarding grants and
31 loans under this section.

33 described in IC 13-20-26, the board shall award not more than four
34 million dollars ($4,000,000) in total to applicants chosen to

36 (1) the recommendations of the department after conducting
37 an evaluation of the proposals submitted under IC 13-20-26-2;
38 and
39 (2) the requirements set forth in subsection (j).
40 (j) In awarding the funds described in subsection (i), the board
41 shall:
42 (1) consult with the department when reviewing the proposals
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150

1 under IC 13-20-26-2;
2 (2) consider the:
3 (A) type; and
4 (B) amount;

31 (d) The amount of the variable recycling fee, if applicable, is the
32 amount determined in STEP FOUR of the following formula:
33 STEP ONE: Multiply the number of pounds of the manufacturer's
34 video display devices sold to households during the immediately
35 preceding program year, as reported in the manufacturer's
36 registration for the program year under IC 13-20.5-1-1(c)(4), by
37 the proportion of sales of video display devices required to be

39 STEP TWO: Subject to subsection (e), add the number of pounds
40 of covered electronic devices recycled by the manufacturer from
41 covered entities during the immediately preceding program year,
42 as reported to the department under IC 13-20.5-3-1(a), to the
2026 IN 277—LS 6849/DI 150

131
1 number of recycling credits the manufacturer elects to use to
2 calculate the variable recycling fee, as reported to the department
3 under IC 13-20.5-3-1(b)(2).
4 STEP THREE: Subtract the number of pounds determined in
5 STEP TWO from the number of pounds determined in STEP
6 ONE.
7 STEP FOUR: Multiply the greater of zero (0) or the number of
8 pounds determined in STEP THREE by the per pound cost of
9 recycling established as follows:
10 (A) Forty cents ($0.40) per pound for manufacturers that
11 recycle less than fifty percent (50%) of the number of pounds
12 determined in STEP ONE.
13 (B) Thirty cents ($0.30) per pound for manufacturers that
14 recycle at least fifty percent (50%) but less than ninety percent
15 (90%) of the number of pounds determined in STEP ONE.
16 (C) Twenty cents ($0.20) per pound for manufacturers that
17 recycle at least ninety percent (90%) of the number of pounds
18 determined in STEP ONE.

20 electronic devices recycled by the manufacturer from covered entities

22 subsection (d), STEP TWO:
23 (1) Except as provided in subdivision (3), the number is
24 multiplied by one and one-tenth (1.1) to the extent that the
25 covered electronic devices were recycled in Indiana.
26 (2) Except as provided in subdivision (3), the number is
27 multiplied by one and five-tenths (1.5) to the extent that the
28 covered electronic devices were recycled from covered entities
29 not located in a metropolitan statistical area, as defined by the
30 federal Office of Management and Budget.
31 (3) The number is multiplied by one and six-tenths (1.6) to the

33 (A) recycled from covered entities not located in a
34 metropolitan statistical area, as defined by the federal Office
35 of Management and Budget; and
36 (B) recycled in Indiana.

42 succeeding program years. A manufacturer may sell all or any part of

1 adjacent to a public highway, state park, state nature preserve, or
